					<div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content"><div class="mw-subjectpageheader">
</div><div class="mw-content-ltr mw-parser-output" lang="en" dir="ltr"><div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">Large bird of prey</div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1320445320">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the bird. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Eagle_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Eagle (disambiguation)">Eagle (disambiguation)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eagles_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Eagles (disambiguation)">Eagles (disambiguation)</a>.</div>

<th colspan="2" class="section-header" style="background:rgb(235,235,210);">Species
</th></tr>
<tr>
<td colspan="2" class="section-content">
<p>See <a href="#Species">text</a>
</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table><style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1337978426">.mw-parser-output table.biota-infobox{text-align:left;width:200px;font-size:100%}body.skin--responsive .mw-parser-output table.biota-infobox td:not(.image-section){padding:2px 10px}.mw-parser-output table.biota-infobox th.section-header{text-align:center}.mw-parser-output table.biota-infobox td.section-content{text-align:left;padding:0 0.25em}.mw-parser-output table.biota-infobox td.list-section{text-align:left;padding:0 0.25em}.mw-parser-output table.biota-infobox td.taxon-section{text-align:left;padding:0 0.25em}.mw-parser-output table.biota-infobox td.image-section{text-align:center;font-size:88%}.mw-parser-output table.biota-infobox table.taxonomy{margin:0 auto;text-align:left;background:transparent;padding:2px}.mw-parser-output table.biota-infobox table.taxonomy tr{vertical-align:top}.mw-parser-output table.biota-infobox table.taxonomy td{padding:1px}body.skin-vector .mw-parser-output table.biota.infobox{margin-top:0.5em}</style>
<p><b>Eagle</b> is the common name for certain large <a href="/wiki/Birds_of_prey" class="mw-redirect" title="Birds of prey">birds of prey</a> within the family of the <a href="/wiki/Accipitridae" title="Accipitridae">Accipitridae</a>. While on a genetic level, only the subfamily <a href="/wiki/Aquilinae" title="Aquilinae">Aquilinae</a> comprises "true eagles", many other species are commonly referred to as eagles, such as the <a href="/wiki/Bald_eagle" title="Bald eagle">bald eagle</a>, and the term generally <a href="/wiki/Paraphyly" title="Paraphyly">carries no taxonomic weight</a>. Most of the 68 <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a> of eagles are from <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-delhoyo&#95;1-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-delhoyo-1"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>1<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Outside this area, just 14 species can be found—two in <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">North America</a>, nine in Central and <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">South America</a>, and three in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>.
</p><p>Eagles are not a natural group but denote essentially any kind of bird of prey large enough to hunt sizeable (about 50&#160;cm long or more overall) <a href="/wiki/Vertebrate" title="Vertebrate">vertebrates</a>.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Etymology">Etymology</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The word "eagle" is borrowed into English from <a href="/wiki/Old_French" title="Old French">Old French</a> <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/aigle#Old_French" class="extiw" title="wikt:aigle">aigle</a></i>, ultimately from <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a> <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/aquila#Latin" class="extiw" title="wikt:aquila">aquila</a></i>. It is cognate with terms such as <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/aigle#French" class="extiw" title="wikt:aigle">aigle</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">Portuguese</a> <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%C3%A1guia#Portuguese" class="extiw" title="wikt:águia">águia</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a> <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%C3%A1guila#Spanish" class="extiw" title="wikt:águila">águila</a></i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Historically, the native <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> term for eagle was "ern" (<a href="/wiki/Old_English_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Old English language">Old English</a>: <i lang="ang"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/earn#Old_English" class="extiw" title="wikt:earn">earn</a></i>), derived from <a href="/wiki/Proto-Germanic" class="mw-redirect" title="Proto-Germanic">Proto-Germanic</a> <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Reconstruction:Proto-Germanic/arnuz" class="extiw" title="wikt:Reconstruction:Proto-Germanic/arnuz">*arnuz</a>, and thus cognate with other synonymous words in Germanic languages such as <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">German</a> <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/Aar#German" class="extiw" title="wikt:Aar">Aar</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Dutch_language" title="Dutch language">Dutch</a> <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/arend#Dutch" class="extiw" title="wikt:arend">arend</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Swedish_language" title="Swedish language">Swedish</a> <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%C3%B6rn#Swedish" class="extiw" title="wikt:örn">örn</a></i> and <a href="/wiki/Gothic_language" title="Gothic language">Gothic</a> <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%F0%90%8C%B0%F0%90%8D%82%F0%90%8C%B0#Gothic" class="extiw" title="wikt:𐌰𐍂𐌰">𐌰𐍂𐌰</a> (<i><span title="Gothic-script transliteration"><span>ara</span></span></i>). The term "ern" or "erne" is still used in <a href="/wiki/Modern_English" title="Modern English">Modern English</a> in reference to some larger species of eagle, in particular the <a href="/wiki/Fish_eagle" class="mw-redirect" title="Fish eagle">fish eagles</a>. While some ornithologists may favor this term as a way to distinguish fish eagles from <a href="/wiki/True_eagle" class="mw-redirect" title="True eagle">true eagles</a>, all species of fish eagle (such as the <a href="/wiki/Bald_eagle" title="Bald eagle">bald eagle</a> and <a href="/wiki/White-tailed_eagle" title="White-tailed eagle">white-tailed eagle</a>) are still commonly referred to as "eagles".
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Description">Description</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Description"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Eagles are large, powerfully-built <a href="/wiki/Birds_of_prey" class="mw-redirect" title="Birds of prey">birds of prey</a>, with heavy heads and beaks. Even the smallest eagles, such as the <a href="/wiki/Booted_eagle" title="Booted eagle">booted eagle</a> (<i>Hieraaetus pennatus</i>), which is comparable in size to a <a href="/wiki/Common_buzzard" title="Common buzzard">common buzzard</a> (<i>Buteo buteo</i>) or <a href="/wiki/Red-tailed_hawk" title="Red-tailed hawk">red-tailed hawk</a> (<i>B. jamaicensis</i>), have relatively longer and more evenly broad wings, and more direct, faster flight, despite the reduced size of their aerodynamic feathers. Most eagles are larger than any other <a href="/wiki/Raptor_(bird)" class="mw-redirect" title="Raptor (bird)">raptors</a>, apart from some <a href="/wiki/Vulture" title="Vulture">vultures</a>. The smallest species of eagle is the <a href="/wiki/Great_Nicobar_serpent_eagle" title="Great Nicobar serpent eagle">Great Nicobar serpent eagle</a> (<i>Spilornis klossi</i>), at 450&#160;g (1&#160;lb) and 40&#160;cm (16&#160;in). The largest species are discussed below. Like all birds of prey, eagles have very large hooked <a href="/wiki/Beak" title="Beak">beaks</a> for ripping flesh from their prey, strong, muscular legs, and powerful <a href="/wiki/Claw" title="Claw">talons</a>.
</p><p>The beak is typically heavier than that of most other birds of prey. Eagles' eyes are extremely powerful. It is estimated that the <a href="/wiki/Wedge-tailed_eagle" title="Wedge-tailed eagle">wedge-tailed eagle</a> has a <a href="/wiki/Visual_acuity" title="Visual acuity">visual acuity</a> twice that of a typical human.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> This acuity enables eagles to spot potential prey from a very long distance. This keen eyesight is primarily attributed to their extremely large pupils which ensure minimal <a href="/wiki/Diffraction" title="Diffraction">diffraction</a> (scattering) of the incoming light. Like most diurnal raptors, eagles have little ability to see <a href="/wiki/Ultraviolet" title="Ultraviolet">ultraviolet</a> light.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The female of all known species of eagles is larger than the male.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Grambo2003&#95;8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Grambo2003-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Eagles normally build their nests, called <a href="/wiki/Bird_nest" title="Bird nest">eyries</a>, in tall trees or on high cliffs. Many species lay two eggs, but the older, larger chick frequently kills its younger sibling once it has hatched. The parents take no action to stop the killing.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-gambo&#95;9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gambo-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-stinson&#95;10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stinson-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
It is said<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (June 2024)">by whom?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> that eagles fly above clouds but this is not true.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2024)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Eagles fly during storms and glide from the wind's pressure. This saves the bird's energy. 
Due to the size and power of many eagle species, they are ranked at the top of the food chain as <a href="/wiki/Apex_predator" title="Apex predator">apex predators</a> in the avian world. The type of prey varies by genus. The <i><a href="/wiki/Haliaeetus" title="Haliaeetus">Haliaeetus</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Icthyophaga" title="Icthyophaga">Icthyophaga</a></i> eagles prefer to capture fish, though the species in the former often capture various animals, especially other <a href="/wiki/Water_bird" title="Water bird">water birds</a>, and are powerful <a href="/wiki/Kleptoparasitism" title="Kleptoparasitism">kleptoparasites</a> of other birds. The snake and serpent eagles of the genera <i><a href="/wiki/Circaetus" title="Circaetus">Circaetus</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Bateleur" title="Bateleur">Terathopius</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Spilornis" title="Spilornis">Spilornis</a></i> predominantly prey on the great diversity of <a href="/wiki/Snake" title="Snake">snakes</a> found in the tropics of Africa and Asia. The eagles of the genus <i><a href="/wiki/Aquila_(genus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Aquila (genus)">Aquila</a></i> are often the top birds of prey in open habitats, taking almost any medium-sized <a href="/wiki/Vertebrate" title="Vertebrate">vertebrate</a> they can catch. Where <i>Aquila</i> eagles are absent, other eagles, such as the <a href="/wiki/Buteoninae" title="Buteoninae">buteonine</a> <a href="/wiki/Black-chested_buzzard-eagle" title="Black-chested buzzard-eagle">black-chested buzzard-eagle</a> of South America, may assume the position of top raptorial predator in open areas. Many other eagles, including the species-rich genus <i><a href="/wiki/Spizaetus" title="Spizaetus">Spizaetus</a></i>, live predominantly in woodlands and forests. These eagles often target various arboreal or ground-dwelling mammals and birds, which are often unsuspectingly ambushed in such dense, knotty environments. Hunting techniques differ among the species and genera, with some individual eagles having engaged in quite varied techniques based on their environment and prey at any given time. Most eagles grab prey without landing and take flight with it, so the prey can be carried to a perch and torn apart.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-RaptorsWorld&#95;11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RaptorsWorld-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Bald_eagle" title="Bald eagle">bald eagle</a> is noted for having flown with the heaviest load verified to be carried by any flying bird, since one eagle flew with a 6.8&#160;kg (15&#160;lb) <a href="/wiki/Mule_deer" title="Mule deer">mule deer</a> fawn.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, a few eagles may target prey considerably heavier than themselves; such prey is too heavy to fly with, thus it is either eaten at the site of the kill or taken in pieces back to a perch or nest. <a href="/wiki/Golden_eagle" title="Golden eagle">Golden</a> and <a href="/wiki/Crowned_eagle" title="Crowned eagle">crowned eagles</a> have killed <a href="/wiki/Ungulate" title="Ungulate">ungulates</a> weighing up to 30&#160;kg (66&#160;lb) and a <a href="/wiki/Martial_eagle" title="Martial eagle">martial eagle</a> even killed a 37&#160;kg (82&#160;lb) <a href="/wiki/Duiker" title="Duiker">duiker</a>, 7–8 times heavier than the preying eagle.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-RaptorsWorld&#95;11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RaptorsWorld-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 67–68">&#58;&#8202;67–68&#8202;</span></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-Watson&#95;14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Watson-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Authors on birds <a href="/wiki/David_Allen_Sibley" title="David Allen Sibley">David Allen Sibley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pete_Dunne_(author)" title="Pete Dunne (author)">Pete Dunne</a>, and Clay Sutton described the behavioral difference between hunting eagles and other birds of prey thus (in this case the bald and golden eagles as compared to other North American raptors):<sup id="cite&#95;ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Old_Abe,_the_live_war_eagle_of_Wisconsin,_from_the_Centennial.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/04/Old_Abe%2C_the_live_war_eagle_of_Wisconsin%2C_from_the_Centennial.jpg" decoding="async" width="92" height="150" class="mw-file-element" data-file-width="92" data-file-height="150" /></a><figcaption>An Eagle named in honor of Abraham Lincoln and was the mascot of 8th Wisconsin Infantry Regiment, at the time of the U.S. Centennial</figcaption></figure>
<blockquote>
<p>They have at least one singular characteristic. It has been observed that most birds of prey look back over their shoulders before striking prey (or shortly thereafter); predation is after all a two-edged sword. All hawks seem to have this habit, from the smallest kestrel to the largest Ferruginous – but not the Eagles.
</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Among the eagles are some of the largest birds of prey: only the <a href="/wiki/Condor" title="Condor">condors</a> and some of the <a href="/wiki/Old_World_vulture" title="Old World vulture">Old World vultures</a> are markedly larger. It is regularly debated<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (June 2024)">according to whom?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> which should be considered the largest species of eagle. They could be measured variously in total length, body mass, or wingspan. Different lifestyle needs among various eagles result in variable measurements from species to species. For example, many forest-dwelling eagles, including the very large <a href="/wiki/Harpy_eagle" title="Harpy eagle">harpy eagle</a>, have relatively short wingspans, a feature necessary for being able to maneuver in quick, short bursts through densely forested habitats.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-RaptorsWorld&#95;11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RaptorsWorld-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Eagles in the genus <i>Aquila</i>, found almost exclusively in open country, are noted for their ability to soar, and have relatively long wings for their size.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-RaptorsWorld&#95;11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RaptorsWorld-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>These lists of the top five eagles are based on weight, length, and wingspan, respectively. Unless otherwise noted by reference, the figures listed are the median reported for each measurement in the guide <i>Raptors of the World</i><sup id="cite&#95;ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> in which only measurements that could be personally verified by the authors were listed.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-RaptorsWorld&#95;11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-RaptorsWorld-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Habitat">Habitat</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Habitat"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The eagles are generally distributed in all types of habitats and nearly all parts of the world. The birds can be found in northern tundra to tropical rainforests and deserts. In North America, bald eagles and golden eagles are very common.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Distribution">Distribution</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Distribution"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Australasian_realm" title="Australasian realm">Australasian</a>
<ul><li>Australia: <a href="/wiki/Wedge-tailed_eagle" title="Wedge-tailed eagle">wedge-tailed eagle</a> (range extends into southern New Guinea), <a href="/wiki/White-bellied_sea-eagle" class="mw-redirect" title="White-bellied sea-eagle">white-bellied sea-eagle</a> (range extends into Asia), <a href="/wiki/Little_eagle" title="Little eagle">little eagle</a>.</li>
<li>New Guinea: <a href="/wiki/Papuan_eagle" title="Papuan eagle">Papuan eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/White-bellied_sea-eagle" class="mw-redirect" title="White-bellied sea-eagle">white-bellied sea-eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pygmy_eagle" title="Pygmy eagle">pygmy eagle</a>.</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nearctic_realm" title="Nearctic realm">Nearctic</a> (USA and Canada): <a href="/wiki/Golden_eagle" title="Golden eagle">golden eagle</a> (also found in Palearctic), <a href="/wiki/Bald_eagle" title="Bald eagle">bald eagle</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Neotropical_realm" title="Neotropical realm">Neotropical</a> (Central and South America): <i><a href="/wiki/Spizaetus" title="Spizaetus">Spizaetus</a></i> (four species), <a href="/wiki/Harpyhaliaetus" class="mw-redirect" title="Harpyhaliaetus">solitary eagles</a> (two spp.), <a href="/wiki/Harpy_eagle" title="Harpy eagle">harpy eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crested_eagle" title="Crested eagle">crested eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Black-chested_buzzard-eagle" title="Black-chested buzzard-eagle">black-chested buzzard-eagle</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Palearctic_realm" title="Palearctic realm">Palearctic</a> (<a href="/wiki/Europe" title="Europe">Europe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northern_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Africa">Northern Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">Asia</a> without <a href="/wiki/South_Asia" title="South Asia">South Asia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Southeast_Asia" title="Southeast Asia">Southeast Asia</a>)
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>: <a href="/wiki/Golden_eagle" title="Golden eagle">Golden eagle</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/White-tailed_eagle" title="White-tailed eagle">White-tailed eagle</a>.</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Subsaharan_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="Subsaharan Africa">Subsaharan Africa</a>: <a href="/wiki/African_fish_eagle" title="African fish eagle">African fish eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Martial_Eagle" class="mw-redirect" title="Martial Eagle">Martial Eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Crowned_eagle" title="Crowned eagle">Crowned eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Verreaux%27s_eagle" title="Verreaux&#39;s eagle">Verreaux's eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tawny_eagle" title="Tawny eagle">Tawny eagle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Long-crested_eagle" title="Long-crested eagle">Long-crested eagle</a></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Groups">Groups</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Groups"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Eagles are often informally divided into four groups.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>a<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-rutledge&#95;23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rutledge-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The snake eagles are placed in the subfamily <a href="/wiki/Circaetinae" title="Circaetinae">Circaetinae</a>. The fish eagles, booted eagles, and harpy eagles have traditionally been placed in the subfamily <a href="/wiki/Buteoninae" title="Buteoninae">Buteoninae</a> together with the buzzard-hawks (buteonine hawks) and harriers. Some authors may treat these groups as tribes of the Buteoninae; Lerner &amp; Mindell<sup id="cite&#95;ref-LM2005&#95;24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LM2005-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> proposed separating the eagle groups into their own subfamilies of <a href="/wiki/Accipitridae" title="Accipitridae">Accipitridae</a>.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Fish_eagles">Fish eagles</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Fish eagles"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Fish eagles (or sea eagles) take fish as a large part of their diets, either fresh or as carrion.
</p><p>Some authors include <i>Gypohierax angolensis</i>, the "vulturine fish eagle" (also called the <a href="/wiki/Palm-nut_vulture" title="Palm-nut vulture">palm-nut vulture</a>) in this group.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rutledge&#95;23-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rutledge-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, genetic analyses indicate it is related to a grouping of <i>Neophron</i>–<i>Gypaetus</i>–<i>Eutriorchis</i> (<a href="/wiki/Egyptian_vulture" title="Egyptian vulture">Egyptian vulture</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bearded_vulture" title="Bearded vulture">bearded vulture</a> (lammergeier), and <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_serpent_eagle" title="Madagascar serpent eagle">Madagascar serpent eagle</a>).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-tol-acciptridae&#95;25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tol-acciptridae-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The fish eagles have a close genetic relationship with <i><a href="/wiki/Haliastur" title="Haliastur">Haliastur</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Milvus" title="Milvus">Milvus</a></i>; the whole group is only distantly related to the <i>Buteo</i> group.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-tol-acciptridae&#95;25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tol-acciptridae-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Fish eagles exist in every continent throughout the world, except for South America.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Although fish eagles can be found in many different places around the world, they have been classified as "Near Threatened". Reasons such as overfishing, pollution, habitat destruction, and the use of pesticides have contributed to the species' rapid population drop.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Booted_eagles">Booted eagles</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Booted eagles"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Booted_eagles" title="Booted eagles">Booted eagles</a> or "true eagles"<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rutledge&#95;23-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rutledge-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-oiseaux-booted&#95;28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oiseaux-booted-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> have feathered tarsi (lower legs).
</p><p>Tribe Aquililae or proposed subfamily Aquilinae. Genera: <i>Aquila</i>, <i>Hieraaetus</i>; <i>Spizaetus</i>, <i>Oroaetus</i>, <i>Spizastur</i>; <i>Nisaetus</i>;<sup id="cite&#95;ref-tol-acciptridae&#95;25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tol-acciptridae-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i>Ictinaetus</i>, <i>Lophoaetus</i>; <i>Polemaetus</i>; and <i>Stephanoaetus</i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rutledge&#95;23-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rutledge-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite&#95;ref-oiseaux-booted&#95;28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-oiseaux-booted-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>See comments under <a href="#Species">eagle species</a> for changes to the composition of these genera.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Snake_eagles">Snake eagles</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Snake eagles"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Most snake or serpent eagles, as the name suggests, primarily prey on snakes.
</p>
<ul><li>Subfamily <a href="/wiki/Circaetinae" title="Circaetinae">Circaetinae</a>. Genera: <i>Circaetus</i>, <i>Spilornis</i>, <i>Dryotriorchis</i>, <i>Terathopius</i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rutledge&#95;23-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rutledge-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li><i>Eutriorchis</i> (subfamily Gypaetinae or Circaetinae).</li></ul>
<p>Despite filling the niche of a snake eagle, genetic studies suggest that the <a href="/wiki/Madagascar_serpent_eagle" title="Madagascar serpent eagle">Madagascar serpent eagle</a> (<i>Eutriorchis</i>) is not related to them.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-tol-acciptridae&#95;25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-tol-acciptridae-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Over several decades, a great deal of research has been done on the &#160;Snake-eagle's diet, which is mainly made up of reptiles, especially snakes. When it comes to catching snakes, it is generally accepted that the bird exhibits generalist feeding behavior, which means it does not hunt down specific types of snakes but rather feeds on them depending on their availability in the wild.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Harpy_eagles">Harpy eagles</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Harpy eagles"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>Harpy eagles<sup id="cite&#95;ref-rutledge&#95;23-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rutledge-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> or "giant forest eagles"<sup id="cite&#95;ref-aae&#95;21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aae-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> are large eagles that inhabit tropical forests. The group contains two to six species, depending on the author. Although these birds occupy similar niches and have traditionally been grouped, they are not all related: the solitary eagles are related to the black hawks and the Philippine eagle to the snake eagles.
</p>
<ul><li>Harpy eagles (proposed subfamily Harpiinae)
<ul><li><i>Harpia harpyja</i>, <a href="/wiki/Harpy_eagle" title="Harpy eagle">harpy eagle</a> ― Central and South America.</li>
<li><i>Morphnus guianensis</i>, <a href="/wiki/Crested_eagle" title="Crested eagle">crested eagle</a> ― Central and South America.</li>
<li><i>Harpyopsis novaeguineae</i>, <a href="/wiki/Papuan_eagle" title="Papuan eagle">Papuan eagle</a> ― New Guinea.</li></ul></li>
<li>Philippine eagle
<ul><li><i>Pithecophaga jefferyi</i>, <a href="/wiki/Philippine_eagle" title="Philippine eagle">Philippine eagle</a> ― Philippines.</li></ul></li>
<li>Solitary eagles
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Chaco_eagle" title="Chaco eagle">Chaco eagle</a> or crowned solitary eagle, <i><a href="/wiki/Buteogallus" title="Buteogallus">Buteogallus</a></i> (formerly <i><a href="/wiki/Harpyhaliaetus" class="mw-redirect" title="Harpyhaliaetus">Harpyhaliaetus</a></i>) <i>coronatus</i> ― South America.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Solitary_eagle" title="Solitary eagle">Solitary eagle</a> or montane solitary eagle, <i><a href="/wiki/Buteogallus" title="Buteogallus">Buteogallus</a></i> (formerly <i><a href="/wiki/Harpyhaliaetus" class="mw-redirect" title="Harpyhaliaetus">Harpyhaliaetus</a></i>) <i>solitarius</i> ― South America.</li></ul></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Species">Species</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Species"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Martial_Eagle_in_Namibia.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8f/Martial_Eagle_in_Namibia.jpg/250px-Martial_Eagle_in_Namibia.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="207" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/8/8f/Martial_Eagle_in_Namibia.jpg/500px-Martial_Eagle_in_Namibia.jpg 2x" data-file-width="622" data-file-height="516" /></a><figcaption>Martial eagle in Namibia</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Pithecophaga_jefferyi.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Pithecophaga_jefferyi.jpg/250px-Pithecophaga_jefferyi.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="307" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/30/Pithecophaga_jefferyi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="388" data-file-height="477" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Philippine_eagle" title="Philippine eagle">Philippine eagle</a> (<i>Pithecophaga jefferyi</i>) in Southern Philippines</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:WedgetailEagleCarrion.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/WedgetailEagleCarrion.jpg/250px-WedgetailEagleCarrion.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="173" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/WedgetailEagleCarrion.jpg/500px-WedgetailEagleCarrion.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="691" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Wedge-tailed_eagle" title="Wedge-tailed eagle">Wedge-tailed eagle</a> in Australia</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%98_%D7%A0%D7%99%D7%A6%D7%99.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%98_%D7%A0%D7%99%D7%A6%D7%99.jpg/250px-%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%98_%D7%A0%D7%99%D7%A6%D7%99.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="173" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%98_%D7%A0%D7%99%D7%A6%D7%99.jpg/500px-%D7%A2%D7%99%D7%98_%D7%A0%D7%99%D7%A6%D7%99.jpg 2x" data-file-width="722" data-file-height="501" /></a><figcaption>Eastern imperial eagle in Israel</figcaption></figure>
<p>Major new research into eagle <a href="/wiki/Taxonomy_(biology)" title="Taxonomy (biology)">taxonomy</a> suggests that the important genera <i>Aquila</i> and <i>Hieraaetus</i> are not composed of nearest relatives, and it is likely that a reclassification of these genera will soon take place, with some species being moved to <i>Lophaetus</i> or <i>Ictinaetus</i>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-LM2005&#95;24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LM2005-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bonelli%27s_eagle" title="Bonelli&#39;s eagle">Bonelli's eagle</a> and the <a href="/wiki/African_hawk-eagle" title="African hawk-eagle">African hawk-eagle</a> have been moved from <i>Hieraaetus</i> to <i>Aquila</i>.</li>
<li>Either the <a href="/wiki/Greater_spotted_eagle" title="Greater spotted eagle">greater spotted eagle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lesser_spotted_eagle" title="Lesser spotted eagle">lesser spotted eagle</a> should move from <i>Aquila</i> to join the <a href="/wiki/Long-crested_eagle" title="Long-crested eagle">long-crested eagle</a> in <i>Lophaetus</i>, or, perhaps better, all three of these species should move to <i>Ictinaetus</i> with the <a href="/wiki/Black_eagle" title="Black eagle">black eagle</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Steppe_eagle" title="Steppe eagle">steppe eagle</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tawny_eagle" title="Tawny eagle">tawny eagle</a>, once thought to be <a href="/wiki/Conspecificity" class="mw-redirect" title="Conspecificity">conspecific</a>, are not even each other's nearest relatives.</li></ul>
<p><b>Family Accipitridae</b>
</p>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320" /><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Accipitridae#Genera" title="Accipitridae">Accipitridae</a></div>
<ul><li><b>Subfamily <a href="/wiki/Aquilinae" title="Aquilinae">Aquilinae</a></b> – true eagles, formerly included in Buteoninae
<ul><li>Genus <i>Stephanoaetus</i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Crowned_eagle" title="Crowned eagle">Crowned eagle</a>, <i>Stephanoaetus coronatus</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Malagasy_crowned_eagle" title="Malagasy crowned eagle">Malagasy crowned eagle</a>, <abbr title="Extinct" aria-label="Extinct" style="border: none; text-decoration: none; cursor: inherit; font-weight: normal; font-style: normal;">†</abbr><i>Stephanoaetus mahery</i></li></ul></li>
<li>Genus <i><a href="/wiki/Nisaetus" title="Nisaetus">Nisaetus</a></i> – previously included in <i>Spizaetus</i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Changeable_hawk-eagle" title="Changeable hawk-eagle">Changeable hawk-eagle</a>, <i>N. cirrhatus</i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Flores_hawk-eagle" title="Flores hawk-eagle">Flores hawk-eagle</a> <i>N. floris</i> – earlier a subspecies, <i>S. c. floris</i></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sulawesi_hawk-eagle" title="Sulawesi hawk-eagle">Sulawesi hawk-eagle</a>, <i>N. lanceolatus</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mountain_hawk-eagle" title="Mountain hawk-eagle">Mountain hawk-eagle</a>, <i>N. nipalensis</i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Legge%27s_hawk-eagle" title="Legge&#39;s hawk-eagle">Legge's hawk-eagle</a>, <i>Nisaetus kelaarti</i> – previously a race of <i>S. nipalensis</i></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Blyth%27s_hawk-eagle" title="Blyth&#39;s hawk-eagle">Blyth's hawk-eagle</a>, <i>N. alboniger</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Javan_hawk-eagle" title="Javan hawk-eagle">Javan hawk-eagle</a>, <i>N. bartelsi</i></li>
<li>(Northern) <a href="/wiki/Philippine_hawk-eagle" title="Philippine hawk-eagle">Philippine hawk-eagle</a>, <i>N. philippensis</i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Pinsker%27s_hawk-eagle" title="Pinsker&#39;s hawk-eagle">Pinsker's hawk-eagle</a> (Southern Philippine hawk-eagle), <i>Nisaetus pinskeri</i> – earlier <i>S. philippensis pinskeri</i></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wallace%27s_hawk-eagle" title="Wallace&#39;s hawk-eagle">Wallace's hawk-eagle</a>, <i>N. nanus</i></li></ul></li>
<li>Genus <i><a href="/wiki/Spizaetus" title="Spizaetus">Spizaetus</a></i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Black_hawk-eagle" title="Black hawk-eagle">Black hawk-eagle</a>, <i>S. tyrannus</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ornate_hawk-eagle" title="Ornate hawk-eagle">Ornate hawk-eagle</a>, <i>S. ornatus</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Black-and-white_hawk-eagle" title="Black-and-white hawk-eagle">Black-and-white hawk-eagle</a>, <i>S. melanoleucus</i> – formerly <i>Spizastur</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Black-and-chestnut_eagle" title="Black-and-chestnut eagle">Black-and-chestnut eagle</a>, <i>S. isidori</i> – formerly <i>Oroaetus</i></li></ul></li>
<li>Genus <i>Lophotriorchis</i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Rufous-bellied_eagle" title="Rufous-bellied eagle">Rufous-bellied eagle</a>, <i>L. kienerii</i> <figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Eagle_Lahore_Zoo_June302005.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Eagle_Lahore_Zoo_June302005.jpg/250px-Eagle_Lahore_Zoo_June302005.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Eagle_Lahore_Zoo_June302005.jpg/500px-Eagle_Lahore_Zoo_June302005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1712" /></a><figcaption>A <a href="/wiki/Steppe_eagle" title="Steppe eagle">steppe eagle</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lahore_Zoo" title="Lahore Zoo">Lahore Zoo</a>, Pakistan</figcaption></figure></li></ul></li>
<li>Genus <i>Polemaetus</i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Martial_eagle" title="Martial eagle">Martial eagle</a>, <i>Polemaetus bellicosus</i></li></ul></li>
<li>Genus <i>Lophaetus</i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Long-crested_eagle" title="Long-crested eagle">Long-crested eagle</a>, <i>Lophaetus occipitalis</i> – possibly belongs in <i>Ictinaetus</i></li></ul></li>
<li>Genus <i>Ictinaetus</i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Black_eagle" title="Black eagle">Black eagle</a>, <i>Ictinaetus malaiensis</i></li></ul></li>
<li>Genus <i><a href="/wiki/Hieraaetus" title="Hieraaetus">Hieraaetus</a></i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Ayres%27s_hawk-eagle" title="Ayres&#39;s hawk-eagle">Ayres's hawk-eagle</a>, <i>H. ayresii</i></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Haast%27s_eagle" title="Haast&#39;s eagle">Haast's eagle</a>, †H. moorei</li></ul></li>
<li>Genus <i><a href="/wiki/Aquila_(genus)" class="mw-redirect" title="Aquila (genus)">Aquila</a></i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bonelli%27s_eagle" title="Bonelli&#39;s eagle">Bonelli's eagle</a>, <i>Aquila fasciata</i> – formerly <i>Hieraaetus fasciatus</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/African_hawk-eagle" title="African hawk-eagle">African hawk-eagle</a>, <i>A. spilogaster</i> – formerly in <i>Hieraaetus</i></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Golden_eagle" title="Golden eagle">Golden eagle</a>, <i>A. chrysaetos</i></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Tawny_eagle" title="Tawny eagle">Tawny eagle</a>, <i>A. rapax</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Greater_spotted_eagle" title="Greater spotted eagle">Greater spotted eagle</a>, <i>A. clanga</i> – to be moved to <i>Lophaetus</i> or <i>Ictinaetus</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lesser_spotted_eagle" title="Lesser spotted eagle">Lesser spotted eagle</a>, <i>A. pomarina</i> – to be moved to <i>Lophaetus</i> or <i>Ictinaetus</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Indian_spotted_eagle" title="Indian spotted eagle">Indian spotted eagle</a>, <i>A. hastata</i> – to be moved to <i>Lophaetus</i> or <i>Ictinaetus</i></li>

<li><a href="/wiki/Gurney%27s_eagle" title="Gurney&#39;s eagle">Gurney's eagle</a>, <i>A. gurneyi</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wahlberg%27s_eagle" title="Wahlberg&#39;s eagle">Wahlberg's eagle</a>, <i>A. wahlbergi</i> – to be moved to <i>Hieraaetus</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wedge-tailed_eagle" title="Wedge-tailed eagle">Wedge-tailed eagle</a>, <i>A. audax</i></li></ul></li></ul></li>
<li><b>Subfamily <a href="/wiki/Buteoninae" title="Buteoninae">Buteoninae</a></b> – hawks, buzzards and erns
<ul><li>Genus <i>Geranoaetus</i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Black-chested_buzzard-eagle" title="Black-chested buzzard-eagle">Black-chested buzzard-eagle</a>, <i>Geranoaetus melanoleucus</i></li></ul></li>

<li>Genus <i><a href="/wiki/Icthyophaga" title="Icthyophaga">Icthyophaga</a></i> – sometimes grouped together with <i>Haliaeetus</i> as Haliaeetinae
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Lesser_fish_eagle" title="Lesser fish eagle">Lesser fish eagle</a>, <i>Icthyophaga humilis</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Grey-headed_fish_eagle" title="Grey-headed fish eagle">Grey-headed fish eagle</a>, <i>I. ichthyaetus</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/African_fish_eagle" title="African fish eagle">African fish eagle</a>, <i>I. vocifer</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/White-bellied_sea_eagle" title="White-bellied sea eagle">White-bellied sea eagle</a>, <i>I. leucogaster</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sanford%27s_sea_eagle" title="Sanford&#39;s sea eagle">Sanford's sea eagle</a>, <i>I. sanfordi</i></li>

<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:CircaetusGallicus.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/CircaetusGallicus.jpg/250px-CircaetusGallicus.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="167" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/57/CircaetusGallicus.jpg/500px-CircaetusGallicus.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2035" data-file-height="1357" /></a><figcaption>Short-toed snake eagle in flight</figcaption></figure>
<ul><li><b>Subfamily <a href="/wiki/Circaetinae" title="Circaetinae">Circaetinae</a></b>: snake-eagles
<ul><li>Genus <i><a href="/wiki/Spilornis" title="Spilornis">Spilornis</a></i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Crested_serpent_eagle" title="Crested serpent eagle">Crested serpent eagle</a>, <i>Spilornis cheela</i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Central_Nicobar_serpent_eagle" class="mw-redirect" title="Central Nicobar serpent eagle">Central Nicobar serpent eagle</a>, <i>S. minimus</i> (subspecies or species)</li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Great_Nicobar_serpent_eagle" title="Great Nicobar serpent eagle">Great Nicobar serpent eagle</a>, <i>S. klossi</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Mountain_serpent_eagle" title="Mountain serpent eagle">Mountain serpent eagle</a>, <i>S. kinabaluensis</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Sulawesi_serpent_eagle" title="Sulawesi serpent eagle">Sulawesi serpent eagle</a>, <i>S. rufipectus</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Spilornis_holospilus" class="mw-redirect" title="Spilornis holospilus">Philippine serpent eagle</a>, <i>S. holospilus</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Andaman_serpent_eagle" title="Andaman serpent eagle">Andaman serpent eagle</a>, <i>S. elgini</i></li></ul></li>
<li>Genus <i>Pithecophaga</i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Philippine_eagle" title="Philippine eagle">Philippine eagle</a>, <i>Pithecophaga jefferyi</i></li></ul></li>
<li>Genus <i>Terathopius</i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Bateleur" title="Bateleur">Bateleur</a>, <i>Terathopius ecaudatus</i></li></ul></li>
<li>Genus <i><a href="/wiki/Circaetus" title="Circaetus">Circaetus</a></i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Short-toed_snake_eagle" title="Short-toed snake eagle">Short-toed snake eagle</a>, <i>Circaetus gallicus</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Beaudouin%27s_snake_eagle" title="Beaudouin&#39;s snake eagle">Beaudouin's snake eagle</a>, <i>Circaetus beaudouini</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Black-chested_snake_eagle" title="Black-chested snake eagle">Black-chested snake eagle</a>, <i>C. pectoralis</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Brown_snake_eagle" title="Brown snake eagle">Brown snake eagle</a>, <i>C. cinereus</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fasciated_snake_eagle" class="mw-redirect" title="Fasciated snake eagle">Fasciated snake eagle</a>, <i>C. fasciolatus</i></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Western_banded_snake_eagle" title="Western banded snake eagle">Western banded snake eagle</a>, <i>C. cinerascens</i></li></ul></li>
<li>Genus <i><a href="/wiki/Dryotriorchis" class="mw-redirect" title="Dryotriorchis">Dryotriorchis</a></i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Congo_serpent_eagle" title="Congo serpent eagle">Congo serpent eagle</a>, <i>D. spectabilis</i></li></ul></li>
<li>Genus <i>Eutriorchis</i> – placement uncertain, may be part of <a href="/wiki/Gypaetinae" title="Gypaetinae">Gypaetinae</a> or <a href="/wiki/Perninae" title="Perninae">Perninae</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Madagascar_serpent_eagle" title="Madagascar serpent eagle">Madagascar serpent eagle</a>, <i>Eutriorchis astur</i></li></ul></li></ul></li>
<li>Subfamily <a href="/wiki/Harpiinae" title="Harpiinae">Harpiinae</a> – harpies, formerly included in Buteoninae
<ul><li>Genus <i>Morphnus</i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Crested_eagle" title="Crested eagle">Crested eagle</a>, <i>Morphnus guianensis</i></li></ul></li>
<li>Genus <i>Harpyopsis</i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Papuan_eagle" title="Papuan eagle">Papuan eagle</a>, <i>Harpyopsis novaeguineae</i></li></ul></li>
<li>Genus <i>Harpia</i>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Harpy_eagle" title="Harpy eagle">Harpy eagle</a>, <i>Harpia harpyja</i></li></ul></li></ul></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="In_culture">In culture</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: In culture"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Lin_Liang-Eagles.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Lin_Liang-Eagles.jpg/250px-Lin_Liang-Eagles.jpg" decoding="async" width="200" height="332" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Lin_Liang-Eagles.jpg/500px-Lin_Liang-Eagles.jpg 2x" data-file-width="976" data-file-height="1618" /></a><figcaption><i>Eagles</i>, a Chinese Ming period painting; Located at the <a href="/wiki/National_Palace_Museum" title="National Palace Museum">National Palace Museum</a></figcaption></figure>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Etymology_2">Etymology</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Etymology"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>The modern English term for the bird is derived from <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>: <i lang="la"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/aquila#Latin" class="extiw" title="wikt:aquila">aquila</a></i> by way of <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/aigle#French" class="extiw" title="wikt:aigle">aigle</a></i>. The origin of <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la">aquila</i></span> is unknown, but it is believed to possibly derive from <span title="Latin-language text"><i lang="la"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/aquilus#Latin" class="extiw" title="wikt:aquilus">aquilus</a></i></span> (meaning dark-colored, swarthy, or blackish) as a reference to the plumage of eagles.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Old_English" title="Old English">Old English</a> used the term <span title="Old English (ca. 450-1100)-language text"><i lang="ang"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/earn#Old_English" class="extiw" title="wikt:earn">earn</a></i></span>, related to Scandinavia's <i><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%C3%B8rn" class="extiw" title="wikt:ørn">ørn</a>/<a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%C3%B6rn" class="extiw" title="wikt:örn">örn</a></i>. It is similar to other <a href="/wiki/Indo-European_languages" title="Indo-European languages">Indo-European</a> terms for "bird" or "eagle", including <a href="/wiki/Greek_language" title="Greek language">Greek</a>: <span lang="el"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E1%BD%84%CF%81%CE%BD%CE%B9%CF%82#Ancient_Greek" class="extiw" title="wikt:ὄρνις">ὄρνις</a></span> (<span title="Greek-language romanization"><i lang="el-Latn"><i>ornís</i></i></span>), <a href="/wiki/Russian_language" title="Russian language">Russian</a>: <span lang="ru"><a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D0%BE%D1%80%D1%91%D0%BB#Russian" class="extiw" title="wikt:орёл">орёл</a></span> (<span title="Russian-language romanization"><i lang="ru-Latn"><i>orël</i></i></span>), and <a href="/wiki/Welsh_language" title="Welsh language">Welsh</a>: <i lang="cy">eryr</i>.
</p><p>In the southern part of <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, near the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Finland" title="Gulf of Finland">Gulf of Finland</a>, is the town of <a href="/wiki/Kotka" title="Kotka">Kotka</a>, which literally means "eagle", while the town of <a href="/wiki/L%27Aquila" title="L&#39;Aquila">L'Aquila</a> in the central part of <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> literally means "the eagle".
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Fountain_top.JPG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Fountain_top.JPG/250px-Fountain_top.JPG" decoding="async" width="250" height="188" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fd/Fountain_top.JPG/500px-Fountain_top.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="2136" /></a><figcaption>The sculpture of eagle at the top of the fountain at <i>Plac Orła Białego</i> in <a href="/wiki/Szczecin" title="Szczecin">Szczecin</a>, Poland</figcaption></figure>
<p>In Britain before 1678, <i>eagle</i> referred specifically to the <a href="/wiki/Golden_eagle" title="Golden eagle">golden eagle</a>, with the other native species, the <a href="/wiki/White-tailed_eagle" title="White-tailed eagle">white-tailed eagle</a>, being known as <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/erne#English" class="extiw" title="wikt:erne"><i>erne</i></a>. The modern name "golden eagle" for <i>aquila chrysaetos</i> was introduced by the naturalist <a href="/wiki/John_Ray" title="John Ray">John Ray</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The village of <a href="/wiki/Eagle,_Lincolnshire" title="Eagle, Lincolnshire">Eagle</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire" title="Lincolnshire">Lincolnshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, has nothing to do with the bird; its name is derived from the Old English words for "oak" and "wood" (compare <i>Oakley</i>).<sup id="cite&#95;ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Religion_and_spirituality">Religion and spirituality</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Religion and spirituality"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-left" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Desfile_Portela_2014_(906185).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Desfile_Portela_2014_%28906185%29.jpg/250px-Desfile_Portela_2014_%28906185%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="166" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Desfile_Portela_2014_%28906185%29.jpg/500px-Desfile_Portela_2014_%28906185%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4256" data-file-height="2832" /></a><figcaption>Representation of an eagle at <a href="/wiki/Rio_Carnival" title="Rio Carnival">Rio Carnival</a>, 2014</figcaption></figure>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="/wiki/File:Garuda_by_Hyougushi_in_Delhi.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Garuda_by_Hyougushi_in_Delhi.jpg/250px-Garuda_by_Hyougushi_in_Delhi.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="284" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Garuda_by_Hyougushi_in_Delhi.jpg/500px-Garuda_by_Hyougushi_in_Delhi.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1232" data-file-height="1840" /></a><figcaption><a href="/wiki/Garuda" title="Garuda">Garuda</a>, the <i><a href="/wiki/Vahana" title="Vahana">vahana</a></i> (mount) of <a href="/wiki/Vishnu" title="Vishnu">Vishnu</a>, depicted with an eagle's beak and wings</figcaption></figure>
<p>In the ancient <a href="/wiki/Sumerian_religion" title="Sumerian religion">Sumerian mythology</a>, the mythical king <a href="/wiki/Etana" title="Etana">Etana</a> was said to have been carried into <a href="/wiki/Heaven" title="Heaven">heaven</a> by an eagle.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Horowitz1998&#95;32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Horowitz1998-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Classical writers such as <a href="/wiki/Lucan" title="Lucan">Lucan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pliny_the_Elder" title="Pliny the Elder">Pliny the Elder</a> claimed that the eagle was able to look directly at the sun, and that they forced their fledglings to do the same. Those that blinked would be cast from the nest. This belief persisted until the <a href="/wiki/Medieval_era" class="mw-redirect" title="Medieval era">Medieval era</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The eagle is the patron animal of the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek_religion" title="Ancient Greek religion">ancient Greek god</a> <a href="/wiki/Zeus" title="Zeus">Zeus</a>. In particular, Zeus was said to have taken the form of an eagle in order to abduct <a href="/wiki/Ganymede_(mythology)" title="Ganymede (mythology)">Ganymede</a>, and there are numerous artistic depictions of the eagle Zeus bearing Ganymede aloft, from Classical times up to the present (see illustrations in the <a href="/wiki/Ganymede_(mythology)" title="Ganymede (mythology)">Ganymede (mythology)</a> page.)<sup id="cite&#95;ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Eagles appear metaphorically in many translations of the <a href="/wiki/Old_Testament" title="Old Testament">Old Testament</a>. God is spoken of as carrying Israel on "eagles' wings" in <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Exodus" title="Book of Exodus">Exodus</a> 19:4, <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Isaiah" title="Book of Isaiah">Isaiah</a> 40:31 compares those who wait on the Lord to flying eagles, and <a href="/wiki/Psalm_103" title="Psalm 103">Psalm 103</a> mentions renewing one's youth "as the eagle". In explaining this rejuvenation, <a href="/wiki/Augustine_of_Hippo" title="Augustine of Hippo">Augustine of Hippo</a> says in his commentary on the <a href="/wiki/Psalms" title="Psalms">Psalms</a> that eagles' beaks overgrow as they age and that they break them against rocks to restore them.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The translation, however, is uncertain: the word in the Hebrew, <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%D7%A0%D7%A9%D7%A8" class="extiw" title="wiktionary:נשר">נשר</a>, can also be translated <a href="/wiki/Vulture" title="Vulture">vulture</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and is listed alongside specific kinds of vulture in <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Leviticus" title="Book of Leviticus">Leviticus</a>' discussion of <a href="/wiki/Kosher_animals" title="Kosher animals">unclean animals</a>.
</p><p>The eagle is also often used in <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a> iconography to represent the <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_John" title="Gospel of John">Gospel of John</a>,<sup id="cite&#95;ref-CathEnc&#95;37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CathEnc-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Eagle_lectern" title="Eagle lectern">eagle-shaped lecterns</a> are common in <a href="/wiki/Anglicanism" title="Anglicanism">Anglican</a> and some <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Roman Catholic churches</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-Delderfield&#95;38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Delderfield-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The eagle was believed to be able to look directly into the sun in the same way that the Gospel of John looks directly at Jesus' divinity, and the great distances the eagle flies represent the spread of the gospel to the ends of the earth.
</p><p>The United States <a href="/wiki/Eagle_feather_law" title="Eagle feather law">eagle feather law</a> stipulates that only individuals of certifiable <a href="/wiki/Native_Americans_in_the_United_States" title="Native Americans in the United States">Native American</a> ancestry enrolled in a federally recognized tribe are legally authorized to obtain eagle feathers for <a href="/wiki/Religion" title="Religion">religious</a> or <a href="/wiki/Spirituality" title="Spirituality">spiritual</a> reasons.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In Canada, the <a href="/wiki/Poaching" title="Poaching">poaching</a> of eagle feathers for the booming U.S. market has sometimes resulted in the arrests of First Nations persons for the crime.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Moche_(culture)" class="mw-redirect" title="Moche (culture)">Moche</a> people of ancient <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a> worshiped the eagle and often depicted eagles in their art.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The golden eagle was sacred to the <a href="/wiki/Aztec_mythology" title="Aztec mythology">Aztec</a> god <a href="/wiki/Huitzilopochtli" class="mw-redirect" title="Huitzilopochtli">Huitzilopochtli</a> while the harpy eagle was sacred to <a href="/wiki/Quetzalcoatl" class="mw-redirect" title="Quetzalcoatl">Quetzalcoatl</a>.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Heraldry">Heraldry</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Eagle&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Heraldry"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>

.multiimageinner span:not(.skin-invert-image):not(.skin-invert):not(.bg-transparent) img{background-color:white}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner multiimageinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Kotka.vaakuna.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Kotka.vaakuna.svg/250px-Kotka.vaakuna.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="230" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/Kotka.vaakuna.svg/500px-Kotka.vaakuna.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="575" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">Coat of arms of <a href="/wiki/Kotka" title="Kotka">Kotka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a></div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><span typeof="mw:File"><a href="/wiki/File:Greater_coat_of_arms_of_the_United_States.svg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Greater_coat_of_arms_of_the_United_States.svg/250px-Greater_coat_of_arms_of_the_United_States.svg.png" decoding="async" width="200" height="211" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/Greater_coat_of_arms_of_the_United_States.svg/500px-Greater_coat_of_arms_of_the_United_States.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="451" data-file-height="476" /></a></span></div><div class="thumbcaption">Coat of arms of the United States</div></div></div></div></div>
<p>Eagles are an exceptionally common symbol in heraldry, being considered the "King of Birds" in contrast to the <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">lion</a>, the "King of Beasts".  Whereas the lion (e.g. England) usually represents authority, the eagle is the symbol of power. They are particularly popular in Germanic countries such as Austria, due to their association with the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Roman_Empire" title="Holy Roman Empire">Holy Roman Empire</a>. The eagle of the Holy Roman Empire was two-headed, supposedly representing the two divisions, <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Roman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Roman Empire">East</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_Roman_Empire" title="Western Roman Empire">West</a>, of the old Roman Empire.  This motif, derived from the Byzantine (Eastern Roman) Empire was also adopted by the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> and is still featured in the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Albania" title="Flag of Albania">Flag of Albania</a>. The Roman eagle was preceded by the eagle of <a href="/wiki/Ptolemaic_Kingdom" title="Ptolemaic Kingdom">Ptolemaic Egypt</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Achaemenid_Empire" title="Achaemenid Empire">Achaemenid Empire</a>. In the coat of arms of <a href="/wiki/Kotka" title="Kotka">Kotka</a>, Finland, the eagle is depicted carrying an <a href="/wiki/Anchor" title="Anchor">anchor</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Caduceus" title="Caduceus">caduceus</a> on its feet.
</p><p>Heraldic eagles are most often found <i>displayed</i>, i.e. with their wings and legs extended. They can also occur <i>close</i>, i.e. with their wings folded, or <i>rising</i>, i.e. about to take flight. The heads, wings, and legs of eagles can also be found independently.
</p><p>Eagles symbolize strength, courage, and independence and are commonly found in the heraldry of many nations across the world. Albania, Andorra, Armenia, Austria, Dagestan, Egypt, Germany, Ghana, Indonesia, Iraq, Jordan, Kazakhstan, Mexico, Montenegro, Nigeria, the Philippines, Poland, Palestine, Panama, Russia, Romania, Serbia, South Sudan, Somaliland, Syria, the United States of America, Yemen, Zambia, and Zimbabwe are the&#160;nations whose coats of arms feature an eagle. The eagle's continuing significance and worldwide appeal as a forceful symbol in national identity and imagery is demonstrated by its widespread usage.<sup id="cite&#95;ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
